[2026-01-26T04:30:53Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 1.	When Cyril Radcliffe partitioned a country he had no prior knowledge about in unseemly haste, he and his team made mistakes. One such mistake was the Berubari Union No. 12 in the Jalpaiguri district of West Bengal. The Radcliffe documents were contradictory; the intent was for that land to be part of India, but some maps showed them in East Pakistan. After negotiations, India and Pakistan agreed to split the territory halfway. Faced with fierce opposition in West Bengal, the President asked the Supreme Court for an advisory opinion. In the famous case “In Re: The Berubari Union” the court ruled in 1960 that a constitutional amendment is necessary to cede territory to another country. It also said that X serves as a key to understanding the minds of the makers of the Constitution, but X is not part of the Constitution itself. ID X.

[2026-01-26T05:10:21Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 9.	The 42nd Amendment was passed in 1976 during the Emergency. Because of its vast size and scope, it has been nicknamed the “X Y.” In addition to changing the Preamble, this amendment sought to push the system towards parliamentary sovereignty and remove checks on legislative power: the President as the head of the executive branch must follow the advise of the Cabinet elected by the legislature, and the courts could no longer check the legislature’s powers to enact laws and amendments. The amendment also introduced fundamental duties for citizens, and sought to nullify the effects of the Supreme Court’s decision in “Kesavananda Bharati vs. State of Kerala.” Some of the excesses of this amendment were later corrected with the 43rd and 44th Amendments, and the Supreme Court’s ruling in “Minverva Mills vs. Union of India” that struck down two clauses of the 42nd Amendment. What is X Y, the nickname of this draconian amendment?

[2026-01-26T05:21:24Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 11.	Many members of the Constituent Assembly were elected based on the provincial elections held in January 1946. In those elections, voting was restricted to property owners. On January 26, 1950, this Assembly transformed into India’s new Parliament. Nehru felt a need to hold quick elections, in the spirit of going back to the electorate at least once every five years. The task of running India’s first election based on universal adult franchise fell to X, appointed as India’s first Y. Historian Ramachandra Guha says about X: “Nehru's haste [in wanting India's first general election] was understandable, but it was viewed with some alarm by the man who had to make the election possible, a man who is *an unsung hero of Indian democracy*. It is a pity we know so little about X.” What we do know: he won the Gold Medal in Mathematics at the University College London, and later among the first recipients of the Padma Bhushan. To enable illiterate voters to exercise their constitutional right to vote, X came up with the idea of prominent symbols on ballot papers, which endures to this day. X served as the first Y for Sudan and Nepal. ID X and Y.
